There are also several causes related to deficiency; whether it arises from familial entanglements or from enemies causing harm, impacting the lung's metal qi and preventing the heavenly way from providing nourishment and clarity, all can be attributed to the blame of fire. However, while fire is singular, deficiency and excess are distinct. Danxi said: Deficient fire can be supplemented, using items like ginseng and astragalus; excess fire can be drained, using herbs like coptis and scutellaria.[36p]

    每见世俗一遇喘家，纯行破气，于太过者当矣，于不及者可乎？余尝论此证因虚而死者十九，因实而死者十一。治实者攻之即效，无所难也。治虚者，补之未必即效，须悠久成功，其间转折进退，良非易也。故辨证不可不急，而辨喘证为尤急也。巢氏、严氏止言实热，独王海藏云：肺气果盛则清肃下行，岂复为喘？皆以火烁真气，气衰而喘。所谓盛者，非肺气也，肺中之火也。斯言高出前古，惜乎但举其端，未能缕悉，请得而详之。气虚而火入于肺者，补气为先，六君子汤、补中益气汤。除虚而火来乘金者，壮水为亟，人味地黄丸。风寒者，解其邪，三拗汤、华盖散。湿气者，利其水，渗湿汤。暑邪者，涤其烦，白虎汤、香薷汤。肺热者，清其上，二冬、二母、甘、桔、栀、芩。痰壅者消之，二陈汤。气郁者疏之，四七汤。饮停者吐之，吐之不愈，木防己汤主之。[37p]

    Whenever I encounter worldly issues and those who suffer from wheezing, a pure condition disrupts the qi. To those who are excessive in their condition, it is rightly so, but what about those who are deficient? I have discussed this and found that nineteen died from deficiency and eleven from excess. To treat excess effectively attacks the root, presenting no difficulty. However, to treat deficiency, supplementation may not yield immediate results; it requires a long-term approach, and the process of adjusting and progressing is not easy. Therefore, it is crucial to distinguish symptoms quickly, especially wheezing symptoms. The Chao and Yan families only speak of excess fire, yet Wang Haizang claims: if lung qi is truly vigorous, it should clear and descend, how could it cause wheezing? All argue that fire consumes the true qi, leading to weakness and wheezing. What is referred to as vigorous is not lung qi but the fire within the lungs. This statement surpasses ancient wisdom; regrettably, it only touches the surface and lacks thorough explanation, so let us elaborate.

    When qi is deficient and fire enters the lungs, one must first supplement qi, using formulas like Six Gentlemen Decoction or Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction. If fire rides on the gold element, it is vital to strengthen water, using methods like Shen Wei Di Huang Wan. For wind-cold, expel the evil with San Ao Decoction or Hua Gai Powder. For dampness, facilitate the water with Shen Shi Decoction. For summer heat, clear the vexation with Bai Hu Decoction or Xiang Ru Decoction. For lung heat, clear the upper parts with Er Dong, Er Mu, Gan, Jiao, Zhi, and Qin. For phlegm obstruction, resolve it with Er Chen Decoction. For qi stagnation, disperse it with Si Qi Decoction. For stagnation of fluids, induce vomiting, but if vomiting does not cure, employ Mu Fang Ji Decoction.[37p]

    火实者清之，白虎汤加(艹舌)蒌仁、枳壳、黄芩神效。肺痈而喘，保金化毒，薏仁、甘草节、桔梗、贝母、防风、金银花、橘红、门冬。肺胀而喘，利水散邪。肺胀之状，咳而上气，喘而烦躁，目如脱状，脉浮大者，越婢加半夏汤；脉浮者心下有水，小青龙汤加石膏主之。肾虚火不归经，导龙入海，八味丸主之。肾虚水邪泛溢，逐水下流，金匮肾气丸。别有哮证，似喘而非，呼吸有声，呀呷不已，良由痰火郁于内，风寒束其外，或因坐卧寒湿，或因酸咸过食，或因积火熏蒸，病根深久，难以卒除，避风寒，节厚味。禁用凉剂，恐风邪难解；禁用热剂，恐痰火易升。理气疏风，勿忘根本，为善治也。宜苏子、枳壳、桔梗、防风、半夏、(艹舌)蒌、茯苓、甘草。[38p]

    Fire is indeed the element of clarity. Baihu Decoction, supplemented with Trichosanthes fruit, bitterorange peel, and Scutellaria, is effective. For lung abscesses causing wheezing, protect the gold and transform toxins with Coix seed, licorice root, Platycodon root, fritillaria, magnolia flower, honeysuckle, tangerine peel, and asparagine. For lung distension with wheezing, promote water and disperse pathogens. Symptoms of lung distension include coughing, shortness of breath, wheezing, restlessness, eyes like bulging, and a floating pulse. In such cases, use the modified Guo Bi Decoction with Pinellia. If the pulse is floating and there's water under the heart, the Xiao Qing Long Decoction plus gypsum should be administered. For kidney deficiency with fire not returning to its pathway, direct the dragon to the sea with Eight Flavor Pill as the main remedy. For kidney deficiency with water evil overflowing, expel water downward with the Jin Kui Shenqi Pill.

    For specific wheezing patterns that may resemble but are not true wheezing, characterized by noisy breathing and persistent sounds, the root cause may be phlegm-fire stagnation internally, with wind-cold constricting externally. This may arise from sitting or lying in dampness, from excess sour and salty food, or from accumulated fire steaming upwards. With deep and longstanding roots, complete eradication is difficult. Avoid wind and cold, and moderate rich flavors.

    Do not use cooling agents, as they may obstruct the resolution of wind evils; avoid heating agents, as they may elevate phlegm-fire. Regulate Qi and disperse wind while not forgetting the fundamentals, for good treatment is achieved this way. Suitable herbs include Perilla seed, bitter orange peel, Platycodon root, magnolia flower, Pinellia, Trichosanthes fruit, Poria, and licorice.[38p]

    如冬月风甚加麻黄，夏月痰多加石膏，挟寒者多用生姜。哮证发于冬初者多先于八九月未寒之时，用大承气下其热，至冬寒时无热可包，此为妙法。如上诸款，皆其大纲。若五脏六腑，七情六气，何在非致喘之由？须知举一隅即以三隅反，方不愧为明通，可以司人之命矣。　　伤寒太阳无汗而喘，太阳阳明合病膈满而喘，俱麻黄汤。邪气壅盛而喘，虽汗而喘不已，宜再发之，麻黄、杏子、石膏。误下太阳利不止，喘而有汗，脉促，葛根黄连黄芩汤。太阳汗后，饮多水停而喘，小青龙去麻黄加杏仁，小腹满加茯苓。太阳下之微喘，表未解也，桂枝汤加厚朴、杏仁。水停心下，肾气乘心，为悸为喘，五苓散。除喘脉伏而逆，理中汤、四逆汤。喘而气促腹满，大柴胡汤。[39p]

    In the winter months, if the wind is fierce, add Mahuang; in the summer months, if there is a lot of phlegm, add Shigao; for those carrying cold, fresh ginger is often used. If wheezing occurs early in winter, it commonly starts in the late summer and early autumn before it turns cold. Utilize Da Chengqi to purge the heat, so that when winter arrives, there is no heat left to contain. This is an excellent method. The aforementioned points cover the broad outlines. If we consider the five organs, six bowels, seven emotions, and six energies, where do they not contribute to wheezing? One must understand that emphasizing one corner implies reflection on all three, to truly be considered insightful, which allows one to govern a person's fate.

    In cases of exogenous cold with a lack of sweating and wheezing, or combined with Yangming syndrome leading to fullness in the diaphragm and wheezing, both call for Mahuang Decoction. If the pathogenic qi is confined and wheezing persists, even after sweating, it is necessary to induce further sweating using Mahuang, Xingzi, and Shigao. If there is misapplication of purging to the Taiyang leading to unending diarrhea, resulting in sweating, and a rapid pulse, use Ge Gen, Huang Lian, and Huang Qinq Decoction. After sweating in the Taiyang, if there is excessive drinking leading to water retention and wheezing, use Xiao Qinglong with the Mahuang removed and add Xingren; if there is fullness in the lower abdomen, add Fuling. If, after purging, there is slight wheezing and the exterior has not resolved, use Gui Zhi Decoction with Houpo and Xingren added. If water is retained under the heart, causing palpitations and wheezing due to kidney qi affecting the heart, use Wu Ling San. To resolve wheezing while the pulse remains depressed and reversed, use Li Zhong Tang and Si Ni Tang. For wheezing with rapid breathing and abdominal fullness, use Da Chai Hu Tang.[39p]

    　　　　医贯 【明　赵献可】

    　　　　　喘论

    　　余按喘与气短有分，则短气是虚，喘是实。然而喘多有不足者，短气间亦有有余者，新病亦有本虚者，不可执论也。　　《金匮》云：实喘者，气实肺盛，呼吸不利，肺窍壅塞，若寸沉实，宜泻肺。虚喘者肾虚，先觉呼吸短气，两胁胀满，左尺大而虚，宜补肾。此肾虚证，非新病虚者乎？　　邪喘者，由肺受邪，伏于肺中，关窍不通，呼吸不利，若寸浮而紧，此外感也。[40p]

    Discussion on Wheezing

    In my view, wheezing and shortness of breath are different; shortness of breath is a manifestation of deficiency, while wheezing is a manifestation of excess. However, wheezing often indicates a deficiency, and shortness of breath can sometimes indicate an excess. New illnesses may also have underlying deficiencies; one should not hold rigid opinions on this matter.

    The "Jin Kui" states that true wheezing arises when the lungs are overactive and obstructed, leading to difficulty in breathing due to blocked lung passages. If the pulse feels deep and firm, one should purge the lungs. Faint wheezing, on the other hand, indicates kidney deficiency, where one first feels short of breath, accompanied by fullness in the sides, with a weak left wrist pulse—this suggests kidney tonification is necessary. This kidney deficiency is not a sign of a new illness?

    Lastly, wheezing due to pathogenic factors arises when evils invade the lungs, becoming lodged within, blocking the passages and causing difficulty in breathing. If the pulse is superficial and tight, this implies an external invasion.[40p]

    亦有六部俱伏者，宜发散则身热退而喘定，此郁证人所难知，非短气中之有余乎？论人之五脏皆有上气，而肺为之主，居于上而为五脏之华盖，通荣卫，合阴阳，升降往来，无过不及，何病之有？若为风寒暑湿所侵，则肺气胀满而为喘，呼吸迫促，坐卧不安，或七情内伤，郁而生痰，或脾胃俱虚，不能摄养。一身之痰，皆能令人喘。　　真知其风寒也，则用仲景青龙汤。真知其暑也，则用白虎汤。真知其湿也，则用胜湿汤。真知其七情郁结也，则用四磨、四七汤。又有木郁、火郁、土郁、金郁、水郁皆能致喘，治者审之【以上俱属有余之证。】　　东垣云：病机云，诸痿喘呕皆属于上。辩云，伤寒家论喘以为火热者，是明有余之邪中于表，寒变为热，心火太旺攻肺，故属于上。又云：膏粱之人，奉养太过，及过爱小儿，亦能积热于上而成喘，宜以甘寒之剂治之。[41p]

    There are also cases in which the six organs are all subdued, and when it is necessary to disperse, the body heats up and the dyspnea subsides. This obstructive condition is difficult for people to recognize; is it not due to the excess in shortness of breath? In discussing the five organs of a person, all have upper qi, with the lungs being the master. They are situated above and form the canopy over the five organs, connecting with the defensive and nutritive qi, balancing yin and yang, allowing for ascent, descent, and movement without excess or deficiency. What illness can arise then? If invaded by wind, cold, summer heat, or dampness, the lung qi becomes distended, leading to dyspnea, rapid breathing, and restlessness in sitting and lying down. This may also arise from internal injury due to the seven emotions, causing stagnation and phlegm, or from deficiency in the spleen and stomach, which fail to nourish properly. Any phlegm in the body can cause dyspnea.

    If one truly understands the presence of wind-cold, then use Zhang Zhongjing's Qinglong Decoction. If one truly understands summer heat, then use Baihu Decoction. If one truly understands dampness, then use Shengshi Decoction. If one truly understands the stagnation of the seven emotions, then use Si Mo or Si Qi Decoction. Additionally, wood stagnation, fire stagnation, earth stagnation, metal stagnation, and water stagnation can all lead to dyspnea; the practitioner must discern these【all of the above fall under the category of excess conditions】.

    Dongyuan says: In terms of pathological mechanisms, various kinds of atrophy, dyspnea, and vomiting all pertain to the upper body. It is further argued that those in the study of cold damage believe that dyspnea caused by fire heat indicates an excess evil present at the surface; cold transforms into heat, and excessive heart fire attacks the lungs, hence it pertains to the upper body. It is also suggested that people who indulge excessively in rich food or overly cherish their children can also accumulate heat above, leading to dyspnea, which should be treated with sweet and cooling remedies.[41p]

    饮食不节，喜怒劳役不时，水谷之寒热，感则害人六腑，皆由中气不足，其(月真)胀腹满，咳喘呕，食不下，宜以大甘辛热之剂治之。《脉经》云：肺盛有余，则咳嗽上气，渴烦心，胸满短气。皆冲脉之火行于胸中而作，系在下焦，非属上也。观东垣之辩，可见起于有余者，病机之邪；杂病者，不足之邪。自是标本判然条析。如遇标病，或汗或吐或下，一药而痰去喘定，奏功如神。粗工以其奏功如神也，执而概施之不足之证，岂不殆哉？楼全善云：凡下痰定喘诸方，施之形实有痰者神效。若虚而脉浮大，按之濇者，不可下之，下之必反剧而死。　　经云：诸喘皆属于上。又谓：诸逆冲上皆属于火。[42p]

    When diet is not regulated, and emotions or labor occur at inappropriate times, the cold and heat of food and water can harm the six viscera, all due to insufficient vital energy. Symptoms like abdominal distension, cough, wheezing, vomiting, and inability to eat should be treated with warm, sweet, and pungent remedies. The "Pulse Classic" states: when the lungs are overflowing, there is coughing and shortness of breath, thirst and restlessness, fullness in the chest, and shortness of breath. These arise from the fire of the ren channel moving in the chest, linked to the lower burner, not belonging to the upper. Observations from Dongyuan’s discussions show there are conditions due to excess and the evil causing illnesses, while complex illnesses arise from deficiency. This clearly distinguishes between the root and branch of disease. When encountering primary illnesses, whether through sweating, vomiting, or purging, a single remedy may expel phlegm and relieve wheezing, producing immediate results. However, practitioners must be cautious with the successful outcomes and should not indiscriminately apply these remedies to deficient symptoms, as this could be dangerous. Liu Quanshan states: all methods for expelling phlegm and stopping wheezing work effectively on those who actually have phlegm. If a patient is deficient and has a floating, large pulse that feels empty upon pressure, it is contraindicated to purge; doing so would certainly worsen the condition and could be fatal. The classics say: all wheezing belongs to the upper. They also state: all counterflow belongs to fire.[42p]

    故河间叙喘病在于热条下。华佗云：肺气盛为喘。《活人书》云：气有余则喘。后代集证类方，不过遵此而已。独王海藏辩云：气盛当认作气衰，有余当认作不足。肺气果盛与有余，则清肃下行，岂复为喘？以其火入于肺，炎烁真阴，衰与不足而为喘焉。所言盛与有余者，非肺之气也，肺中之火也。海藏之辩，超出前人，发千古之精奥，惜乎起其端，未竟其火之所由来。愚谓火之有余，水之不足也；阳之有余，阴之不足也。凡诸冲逆之火，皆下焦冲任相火出于肝肾者也，故曰冲逆。肾水虚衰，相火偏胜，壮火食气，消铄肺金，乌得而不喘焉？丹溪云：喘有阴虚，自小腹下火起而上，宜四物汤加青黛、竹沥、陈皮，入童便煎服。[43p]

    Therefore, in Hejian, the wheezing condition is due to the heat below. Hua Tuo said: "When the lung qi is abundant, there is wheezing." The "Book of Living" states: "Excess qi leads to wheezing." Later compilations of herbal evidence merely follow this. Only Wang Haizang argues that when qi is abundant, it should be recognized as qi being deficient; when there is excess, it should be understood as insufficient. If lung qi is indeed abundant and excessive, then the clear and descending actions should not lead to wheezing, right? Because the fire invades the lungs, scorching the true yin, the condition of deficiency arises as wheezing. What is described as abundance and excess is not the qi of the lungs, but the fire within them. Haizang's argument surpasses those before him, revealing the profound truths of all ages. It is regrettable that it only touches upon the beginnings without tracing the source of the fire. I foolishly believe that excess fire corresponds to insufficient water; excess yang corresponds to insufficient yin. All the fiery reversals arise from the lower jiao where the heartfire is emitted from the liver and kidneys, hence they are termed "reversed." When kidney water is deficient and declining, the heartfire rises too strongly, consuming the lung metal. How can there be no wheezing? Danxi said: "Wheezing has its roots in yin deficiency, with fire rising from the lower abdomen. It is suitable to use the Siwu Decoction with additions of Qingdai, Zhu Li, and Chen Pi, boiled with a child's urine for consumption."[43p]

    如挟痰喘者，四物加枳壳、半夏，补阴以化痰。夫谓阴虚发喘，丹溪实发前人之所未发。但如此治法，实流弊于后人。盖阴虚者，肾中之真阴虚也，岂四物阴血之谓乎？其火起者下焦龙雷之火也，岂寒凉所能降乎？其间有有痰者，有无痰者，水挟木火而上也，岂竹沥、枳、半之能化乎？须用六味地黄加门冬、五味大剂煎饮，以壮水之主，则水升火降而喘自定矣。盖缘阴水虚故有火，有火则有痰，有痰则咳嗽，咳嗽之甚则喘，当与前阴虚相火论参看。　　又有一等似火而非火，似喘而非喘者，经曰：少阴所谓呕咳上气喘者，阴气在下，阳气在上，诸阳气浮，无所依归，故上气喘也。[44p]

    If someone has a phlegm-ridden cough, they should take the Four Substances decoction with bitter orange and pinellia to nourish the yin and transform the phlegm. It is said that if the yin is deficient, it causes coughing, which is something that past practitioners did not realize. However, this method has led to misconceptions for future practitioners. The true deficiency lies in the essence of the kidneys; it is not simply about nourishing the blood with the Four Substances decoction. The fire that arises is from the lower burner, not something that can be suppressed by cold. Among patients, some have phlegm while others do not; the water rises with the wood and fire, and one cannot rely on bamboo sap, bitter orange, or pinellia to transform it. It is necessary to use the Six Flavor Rehmannia decoction with ophiopogon and a strong dose of five flavors to reinforce the water element, thus allowing the water to rise and the fire to descend, stabilizing the cough. This happens because the deficiency of the yin water generates fire; with fire, there is phlegm; with phlegm, there is coughing, which becomes more severe and leads to wheezing. This should be compared with the previously mentioned yin deficiency and its associated fire.

    Additionally, there is another condition that resembles fire but is not fire, that resembles coughing but is not coughing. The classics state that the lesser yin refers to nausea, coughing, and wheezing; it occurs when the yin energy is below and the yang energy is above. When all the yang energies float without a place to settle, that is why there is wheezing.[44p]

    《黄帝针经》云：胃络不和，喘出于阳明之气逆。阳明之气下行，今逆而上行，故喘。真元耗损，喘出于肾气之上奔，其人平日若无病，但觉气喘，非气喘也，乃气不归元也。规其外证，四肢厥逆面赤，而烦躁恶热，似火非火也，乃命门真元之火，离其宫而不归也。察其脉两寸虽浮大而数，两尺微而无力，或似有而无为辨耳。不知者，以其有火也，少用凉药以清之；以其喘急难禁也，佐以四磨之类以宽之。下咽之后，似觉稍快，少顷依然。岂知宽一分，更耗一分，甚有见其稍快，误认药力欠到，倍进寒凉快气之剂，立见其毙矣。何也？盖阴虚至喘，去死不远矣。幸几希一线，牵带在命门之根，尚尔留连。[45p]

    The "Huangdi Needle Classic" states: If the stomach channels are not in harmony, wheezing occurs due to the rebellious qi of the Yangming. The qi of Yangming is supposed to descend, but now it rises upwards, hence the wheezing. When the True Yuan is depleted, wheezing issues arise from the kidney qi surging upwards. Such a person may not appear ill on ordinary days but feels short of breath, which is not actually true wheezing but qi that does not return to its origin.

    Observing the external symptoms, the limbs are cold, the face is red, and there is irritability and aversion to heat, though it seems like fire, it is actually the fire of the True Yuan of the Mingmen, having left its palace without returning. Examining the pulse, though it feels large and rapid at the two-inch mark, at the two-foot mark it is weak and may feel present but is actually absent. Those who do not understand might think there is heat and use cooling herbs to clear it; thinking that the wheezing is urgent, they might assist with herbs like Si Mo to alleviate it. After swallowing, there seems to be slight improvement, but after a moment, it remains the same.

    Little do they know that easing it by a little further depletes it even more. Indeed, seeing slight improvement, they mistakenly believe the medicine’s effect is insufficient and double the intake of cool, qi-promoting agents, immediately witnessing fatal results. Why is this? It is because when yin is deficient leading to wheezing, death is not far away. Fortunately, there is a thread of hope, tethered at the root of the Mingmen, lingering just a bit longer.[45p]

    善治者，能求其绪，而以助元接真镇坠之药，俾其返本归原，或可回生，然亦不可峻骤也。且先以八味丸、安肾丸、养正丹之类煎人参生脉散送下。觉气若稍定，然后以大剂参芪补剂，加破故纸、阿胶、牛膝等以镇于下，又以八味丸加河车为丸。日夜遇饥则吞服方可。然犹未也，须远房帏，绝色欲，经年积月，方可保全。不守此禁，终亦必亡而已。予论至此，可为寒心。聪明男子，当自治未病，毋蹈此危机。　　又有一等火郁之证，六脉俱濇，甚至沉伏，四肢悉寒，甚至厥逆拂拂，气促而喘，却似有余而脉不紧数，欲作阴虚而按尺鼓指，知为畜郁已久，阳气拂遏，不能营运于表，以致身冷脉微，而闷乱喘急。[46p]

    A good ruler can seek the root cause and use remedies to assist in restoring the original state, allowing for a possible revival; however, this must not be done hastily. First, one should use compounds like the Eight-Treasure Pill, the Kidney-Calming Pill, and the Nourishing Essence Pill, along with ginseng and Shengmai Powder to help settle the energy. When the energy is somewhat stabilized, then a larger dose of ginseng and astragalus should be supplemented with additional ingredients like broken old paper, donkey-hide gelatin, and ox knee to calm the lower body. Additionally, the Eight-Treasure Pill should be combined with river vehicle to form pills, to be swallowed during bouts of hunger, day and night. Yet, this is still not sufficient; one must maintain separation from distractions and abstain from desires for many years to ensure preservation. Those who do not adhere to this prohibition will inevitably face demise. I express this for consideration, hoping that wise men will take preventive measures before illness strikes, rather than falling into this crisis.

    Furthermore, there is another type of condition characterized by excessive heat, where all six pulses are weak, even submerged, with cold limbs that may lead to reverse coldness, breathlessness, and anxiety as if there is excess, yet the pulse is not tight. This indicates a long-standing accumulation of heat; the yang energy is impeded and cannot circulate to the surface, resulting in coldness of the body and a weak pulse, accompanied by confusion and breathlessness.[46p]

    当此之时，不可以寒药下之，又不可以热药投之。惟逍遥散加茱、连之类，宣散畜热，得汗而愈；愈后乃以六味地黄，养阴和阳方佳。此谓火郁则发之，木郁则达之，即《金匮》所云：六脉沉伏宜发散则热退而喘定是也。经曰：火郁之发，民病少气，治以诸凉。或问喘者多不能卧，何也？《素问》逆调论云：夫不得卧，卧则喘者，水气之客也。夫水者，循津液而流也。肾者水脏，主津液主卧与喘也。东垣云：病人不得卧，卧则喘者，水气逆行乘于肺，肺得水而浮，使气不得流通也。仲景云：短气皆属饮。　　已上详论阴虚发喘之证治。若阳虚致喘，东垣已详尽矣；外感发喘，仲景已详尽矣。兹为补天立论，故加意于八味、六味云。[47p]

    At this time, one should not use cold herbs, nor should one use hot herbs. Only a blend of Xiao Yao San with substances like zhu and lian can disperse internal heat and promote sweating for recovery. After recovery, one should use Liu Wei Di Huang Wan to nourish yin and harmonize yang, which is best. This means that when fire is congested, it should be released, and when wood is distraught, it should be allowed to flow. This aligns with the "Jin Kui" which states that when the six pulses are depressed, they should be released so that heat recedes and breath stabilizes. The classic says: "When fire is congested, people suffer from reduced energy, treated with cooling methods."

    If asked why those with breath issues often cannot lie down, the "Suwen" indicates that those who cannot lie down and experience breathlessness are troubled by water qi. Water flows along the channels of body fluids. The kidneys are the water organ, governing body fluids, lying down, and breathing. Dong Yuan states that if a patient cannot lie down, but breathes heavily while lying down, it indicates that water qi is counteracting and affecting the lungs, causing the lungs to become waterlogged and preventing proper airflow. Zhongjing states that shortness of breath is associated with fluid retention.

    The above discusses in detail the diagnosis and treatment of breathlessness due to yin deficiency. If breathlessness arises from yang deficiency, Dong Yuan has thoroughly covered this. For externally contracted breathlessness, Zhongjing has also addressed it completely. This is provided to establish foundational principles, hence additional emphasis is placed on Ba Wei and Liu Wei.[47p]

    　　　　景岳全书 【明　张介宾】

    　　　　　论证

    　　气喘之病，最为危候，治失其要，鲜不误人。欲辨之者，亦惟二证而已。所谓二证者，一曰实喘，一曰虚喘也。此二证相反，不可混也。然则何以辨之？盖实喘者有邪，邪气实也；虚喘者无邪，元气虚也。实喘者，气长而有余；虚喘者，气短而不续。实喘者，胸胀气粗，声高息涌，膨膨然若不能容，惟呼出为快也；虚喘慌张气怯，声低息短，皇皇然若气欲断，提之若不能升，吞之若不相及，劳动则甚而惟急促似喘，但得引长一息为快也。此其一为真喘，一为似喘。真喘者其责在肺，似喘者其责在肾。[48p]

    On Breathlessness

    The disease of breathlessness is the most critical condition; if not treated correctly, it is rarely without consequence. To distinguish it, there are essentially two types. The first type is termed "true breathlessness," and the second type is "false breathlessness." These two types are opposites and should not be confused.

    So how do we distinguish between them? True breathlessness is characterized by the presence of an external pathogen, while false breathlessness results from an absence of such a pathogen, relying instead on a deficiency of vital energy. In true breathlessness, the breath is prolonged and abundant; in false breathlessness, the breath is short and unsteady.

    In true breathlessness, the chest feels swollen and the breath is coarse, the sound is loud and the panting is forceful, creating a sensation of fullness that can only be relieved by exhaling; in false breathlessness, the breath is quick and weak, the sound is low and the inhalation is short, creating a feeling of urgency as if the breath is about to stop, rising as if it cannot ascend, and swallowing as if it cannot connect, worsening with exertion and appearing hurriedly panting, only finding slight relief by extending a single breath.

    Thus, one form is true breathlessness, and the other is mimic breathlessness. True breathlessness is attributed to the lungs, while mimic breathlessness is attributed to the kidneys.[48p]

    何也？盖肺为气之主，肾为气之根，肺主皮毛而居上焦，故邪气犯之，则上焦气壅而为喘。气之壅滞者，宜清宜破也。肾主精髓而在下焦，若真阴亏损，精不化气，则下不上交而为促。促者断之基也。气既短促，而再加消散，如压卵矣。且气盛有邪之脉，必滑数有力；而气虚无邪之脉，必微弱无神，此脉候之有不同也。其有外见浮洪，或芤大至极，而稍按即无者，此正无根之脉也。或往来弦甚而极大极数，全无和缓者，此正胃气之败也，俱为大虚之候。但脉之微弱者，其真虚易知，而脉之浮空弦搏者，其假实难辨。然而轻重之分，亦惟于此而可察矣。盖其微弱者，犹顺而易医，浮空者最险而多变。若弦强之甚，则为真脏已见，不可为也。[49p]

    What is it? The lung is the master of qi, and the kidney is the root of qi. The lung governs the skin and hair and is located in the upper jiao. Thus, when pathogenic factors invade, qi in the upper jiao becomes congested, leading to wheezing. When qi is obstructed, it should be cleared and dispersed. The kidney governs essence and is located in the lower jiao. If true yin is deficient and essence cannot transform into qi, then there is an obstruction in the upward exchange, resulting in shortness of breath. Shortness of breath is the basis for distress. When qi is already short and further dissipated, it is like pressing on an egg. Moreover, when qi is abundant, the pulse will be slippery, rapid, and strong; whereas when qi is deficient with no pathogenic factors, the pulse will be weak and lacking spirit. This illustrates the difference in pulse conditions. If one sees a floating and surging pulse, or a greatly wide pulse that disappears with slight pressure, this indicates a pulse with no foundation. If the pulse fluctuates strongly and is exceedingly large and rapid, yet is entirely lacking in harmony, it signals a defeat of the stomach qi, both representing significant deficiency. However, the weakness of the pulse is easily recognized as true deficiency, while a floating and hollow pulse can be difficult to distinguish between true and false fullness. Nevertheless, the distinction in intensity can be observed here. The weak pulse is still manageable and easily treated, while the floating hollow pulse is the most perilous and variable. If the string-like pulse is excessively strong, it indicates a palpable disturbance in the zang organs and is not to be treated.[49p]

    　　　　　论治

    　　凡虚喘之证，无非由气虚耳。气虚之喘，十居七八，但察其外无风邪，内无实热而喘者，即皆虚喘之证。若脾肺气虚者，不过在中上二焦，化源未亏，其病犹浅。若肝肾气虚，则病出下焦，而本末俱病，其病则深，此当速救其根，以接助真气，庶可回生也。其有病久而加以喘者，或久服消痰散气等剂而反加喘者，或上为喘咳而下为泄泻者，或妇人产后亡血过多则营气暴竭，孤阳无依而为喘者，此名孤阳绝阴，剥极之候，已为难治，更毋蹈剥肤之戒也。[50p]

    On Governance

    All cases of wheezing are fundamentally due to qi deficiency. Among those with qi deficiency-induced wheezing, seven or eight out of ten show no external wind pathogens and no internal heat, indicating they are cases of weak wheezing. If the deficiency is in the spleen and lungs, it is confined to the upper jiao, where the transformation source is not yet depleted, making the condition relatively mild. However, if the deficiency is in the liver and kidneys, the illness arises from the lower jiao, affecting both root and branch, making the condition more severe. It is crucial to promptly address the root to support the true qi, thus allowing for recovery. In instances where the illness is prolonged and accompanied by worsening wheezing, or if chronic use of phlegm-resolving and qi-dispersing medications exacerbates the wheezing, or if there is wheezing above and diarrhea below, or if a woman experiences excessive blood loss after childbirth leading to a severe deficiency of nutritive qi, where the solitary yang is unsupported causing wheezing, this is termed the state of solitary yang devoid of yin, a condition of extreme depletion, which becomes difficult to treat. One must be wary of further depleting the surface.[50p]

    　　虚喘证，其人别无风寒咳嗽等疾，而忽见气短似喘，或但经微劳，或饥时即见喘促，或于精泄之后，或于大汗之后，或于大小便之后，或大病之后，或妇人月期之后，而喘促愈甚，或气道噎塞，上下若不相续，势剧垂危者，但察其表里无邪，脉息微弱无力，而诸病若此，悉宜以贞元饮主之，加减如本方，其效如神。此外如小营煎、大营煎、大补元煎之类，俱可择用。经曰：肝苦急，急食甘以缓之，即此之类。
    若大便溏泄，兼下寒者，宜右归饮、右归丸、圣朮煎之类主之。脾肺气虚，上焦微热微渴而作喘者，宜生脉散主之。或但以气虚而无热者，惟独参汤为宜。若火烁肺金，上焦热甚，烦渴多汗，气虚作喘者，宜人参白虎汤主之。若火在阴分，宜玉女煎主之。然惟夏月或有此证，若阴虚自小腹火气上冲而喘者，宜补阴降火，以六味地黄汤加黄蘗、知母之类主之。　　水病为喘者，以肾邪干肺也。[51p]

    The condition of qi shortness, characterized by a person who shows no signs of cold or cough, suddenly experiences labored breathing. This may occur after slight exertion, during hunger, after seminal emission, after heavy sweating, or following urination or defecation. It may also worsen after a significant illness or for women after their menstrual period. If there is a sense of obstruction in the airways, making it seem as if the upper and lower parts are not connected, and if the condition seems critical, one should simply note that there are no external or internal pathogens, and the pulse is weak and feeble. In such cases, one should use the Zhengyuan decoction with adjustments as necessary, yielding divine results. Furthermore, preparations like Xiaoying decoction, Daying decoction, and Dabu Yuan decoction can also be selected for use. The classics state that if the liver feels tight, one should consume sweet foods to alleviate it, which is in line with this condition.

    If there is diarrhea with coldness accompanying it, it is advisable to use the Right Returning Decoction, Right Returning Pill, or Shengzhu Decoction. If there is deficiency of spleen and lung qi, with slight heat and thirst in the upper burner causing wheezing, one should use the Shengmai Powder. If there is simply qi deficiency without heat, only Ginseng Decoction is appropriate. If the fire scorches the lung's metal element, and there is significant heat in the upper burner, frequent thirst, and sweating, leading to wheezing due to qi deficiency, one should use the Ren Shen Bai Hu Decoction. If fire resides in the yin aspects, one should use the Jade Woman Decoction. Nevertheless, this condition typically arises in summer; if yin deficiency causes fire from the lower abdomen to surge upwards and lead to wheezing, one should tonify yin and reduce fire, using the Liu Wei Di Huang Decoction with additions such as Huangbo and Zhimu.

    Wheezing due to water disorders is linked to kidney evils affecting the lungs.[51p]

    然水不能化，而子病及母，使非精气之败，何以至此？此其虚者十九而间乎虚中挟实，则或有之耳。故凡治水喘者，不宜妄用攻击之药，当求肿胀门诸法治之，肿退而喘自定。古法治心下有水气，上乘于肺，喘而不得卧者，以直指神秘汤主之。但此汤性用多主气分，若水因气滞者，用之则可。若水因气虚者，当以加减金匮肾气汤主之。老弱人久病气虚发喘者，但当以养肺为主。凡阴盛者，宜温养之，如人参、当归、姜、桂、甘草，或加以芪朮之属。阳胜者宜滋养之，如人参、熟地、麦冬、阿胶、五味子、梨浆、牛乳之属。[52p]

    However, if the water cannot transform, and the child suffers along with the mother, causing a failure of vital essence, how did it come to this? It is the vacuity that is nineteen parts, mixed within, but containing some solidity; thus, it may occasionally occur. Therefore, for treating water retention and wheezing, it is unwise to recklessly use aggressive medications. One should seek methods that target swelling; once the swelling subsides, the wheezing will stabilize on its own. The ancient method for treating water accumulation below the heart, which rises to the lungs causing wheezing and inability to lie down, is primarily to use the mysterious herbal formula. However, this formula predominantly addresses the vital energy aspect. If the water issue arises from Qi stagnation, it may be used. If it arises from Qi deficiency, one should employ the modified Shenqi Decoction. For the elderly and weak with prolonged illness leading to Qi deficiency and wheezing, one should primarily focus on nourishing the lungs. For those with excessive Yin, it is advisable to warm and nourish with ingredients such as ginseng, angelica, ginger, cinnamon, and licorice, or to include astragalus and poria. For those with excessive Yang, it is advisable to nourish with ingredients such as ginseng, cooked rehmannia, ophiopogon, ejiao, schisandra, pear jelly, and dairy products.[52p]

    　　关格之证为喘者，如六节脏象论曰：人迎四盛已上为格阳，寸口四盛已上为关阴，人迎与寸口俱盛四倍以上为关格。此关格之证，以脉言不以病言也。今人之患此者颇多，而人多不知。且近时察脉者，不论人迎惟在寸口，但其两手之脉，浮弦至极大至四倍以上者，便是此证，其病必虚里跳动而气喘不已，此之喘状，多无咳嗽，但觉胸膈舂舂，似胀非胀，似短非短，微劳则喘甚，多言亦喘甚，甚至通身振振，慌张不宁，此必情欲伤阴，以致元气无根，孤阳离剧之候也，多不可治。[53p]

    The evidence for the condition of “guan ge” manifested as breathlessness is described in the "Treatise on the Six Meridians and Organ Symptoms." It states that when the "renying" pulse is strong at four levels or above, it indicates a yang condition, while when the "cunkou" pulse is strong at four levels or above, it indicates a yin condition. If both the renying and cunkou pulses are strong at four times above normal, it confirms the condition of guan ge. This diagnosis is based on the pulse rather than the illness itself. Currently, there are many individuals suffering from this condition, yet many remain unaware. Furthermore, recent practitioners of pulse diagnosis tend to focus exclusively on the cunkou pulse, disregarding the renying. If the pulses in both hands are excessively strong—floating and string-like to an extreme, four times or more—this indicates such a condition. The patient often experiences a restless, uneasy breathlessness, which is characterized by a feeling of pressure in the chest that can seem like swelling but is not truly swollen. The breath may feel short yet is not truly so, and even slight exertion or speaking can exacerbate the breathlessness. There may also be tremors throughout the body, along with feelings of anxiety and unrest. This condition is primarily due to emotional disturbances harming the yin, leading to a lack of foundational vital energy, resulting in a situation where the solitary yang is separated and chaotic. It is often difficult to treat.[53p]

    　　凡病喘促，但察其脉息微弱细濇者，必阴中之阳虚也。或浮大弦芤，按之空虚者，必阳中之阴虚也。大凡喘息不得卧，而脉见如此者，皆元气大虚，去死不远之候。若妄加消伐，必增剧而危。若用苦寒或攻下之，无不即死。　　实喘之证，以邪实在肺也。肺之实邪，非风寒则火邪耳。盖风寒之邪，必受自皮毛，所以入肺而为喘。火之炽盛，金必受伤，故亦以病肺而为喘。治风寒之实喘，宜以温散；治火热之实喘，宜以寒凉。[54p]

    In the case of shortness of breath, if the pulse is weak and faint, it indicates a deficiency of yin within yang. If the pulse is floating, large, or hollow, and feels empty upon pressure, this indicates a deficiency of yin within yang. Generally, if the patient cannot lie down due to the difficulty in breathing and the pulse is of such nature, it signifies a severe deficiency of vital energy and is close to death. If one rashly administers draining treatments, it will only exacerbate the condition and lead to danger. The use of bitter cold or purgatives will certainly result in immediate death.

    In the case of true shortness of breath, the pathogenic factor resides in the lungs. The pathogenic factor affecting the lungs is either wind-cold or fire. The wind-cold pathogen must be contracted from the surface of the skin, thus it enters the lungs and causes breathing difficulties. When fire is in excess, it injures metal (the lungs) and leads to shortness of breath as well. To treat wind-cold causing true shortness of breath, one should use warming and dispersing methods; to treat fire-heat causing true shortness of breath, one should use cooling methods.[54p]

    又有痰喘之说，前人皆曰治痰，不知痰岂能喘，而必有所以生痰者，此当求其本而治之。凡风寒外感，邪实于肺，而咳喘并作者，宜六安煎加细辛或苏叶主之。若冬月风寒感甚者，于本方加麻黄亦可，或用小青龙汤、华盖散、三拗汤之类主之。外有风寒，内兼微火而喘者，宜黄芩半夏汤主之。兼阳明火盛而以寒包热者，宜凉而兼散，以大青龙汤或五虎汤、赵婢加半夏汤之类主之。外无风寒。而惟火盛作喘，或虽有微寒而所重在火者，宜桑白皮汤或抽薪饮之类主之。[55p]

    There is also a discussion on phlegm and wheezing. Previous experts all stated to treat phlegm, not knowing that phlegm cannot wheeze by itself, and that there must be a cause for the production of phlegm. Therefore, one should seek the root cause and treat it. Generally, when one is invaded by wind and cold from the outside, with obstruction in the lungs leading to cough and wheezing, one should use Liu'an Decoction with a supplement of fine root or perilla leaves. If the invasion of wind and cold is severe in winter, one can add ephedra to the original formula, or use Xiao Qing Long Decoction, Hua Gai Powder, or San Ao Decoction types to address it. For cases with external wind and cold coupled with slight internal heat causing wheezing, Huang Qin Ban Xia Decoction should be used. If there is a combination of excessive Yangming fire and heat wrapped in cold, one should use cooling yet dispersing methods, such as Da Qing Long Decoction or Wu Hu Decoction, or Zhao Bi with Ban Xia Decoction types. If there is no external wind or cold, but only excessive fire causing wheezing, or even if there is slight cold but the emphasis is on fire, one should use Sang Bai Pi Decoction or Chou Xin Drink types to address it.[55p]

    　　痰盛作喘者，虽宜治痰，如二陈汤、六安煎、导痰汤、千缗汤、滚痰丸、抱龙丸之类，皆可治实痰之喘也。六君子汤、金水六君煎之类，皆可治虚痰之喘也。然痰之为病，亦惟为病之标耳，犹必有生痰之本。故凡痰因火动者，必须先治其火；痰因寒生者，必须先去其寒。至于或因气逆，或因风邪，或因湿滞，或因脾肾虚弱，有一于此，皆能生痰。使欲治痰而不治其所以痰，则痰终不能治，而喘何以愈哉？　　气分受邪，上焦气实作喘，或怒气郁结伤肝，而人壮力强，胀满脉实者，但破其气而喘自愈，宜廓清饮、四疮饮、四七汤、萝卜子汤、苏子降气汤之类主之。或阳明气秘不通而胀满者，可微利之。[56p]

    When phlegm is abundant and causes wheezing, it is appropriate to treat the phlegm with formulas such as Erchen Decoction, Liu’an Decoction, Daotan Decoction, Qianqin Decoction, Gunphlegm Pill, or Baolong Pill, all of which can address wheezing caused by excessive phlegm. Formulas like Liu Jun Zi Decoction and Jin Shui Liu Jun Decoction can treat wheezing due to deficient phlegm. However, phlegm itself is merely a symptom of an underlying condition, so there must be a source causing the phlegm. Therefore, if phlegm arises from heat, the heat must be treated first; if from cold, the cold must be expelled first. Additionally, phlegm can also be generated from repressed qi, wind pathogens, damp stagnation, or weakness in the spleen and kidneys. If any of these factors contribute, they can lead to phlegm formation. If one attempts to treat phlegm without addressing its root cause, then the phlegm will never be resolved, and the wheezing cannot be cured.

    If the qi level is affected by pathogens, and there is excess qi in the upper jiao causing wheezing, or if emotional stress has caused liver injury, a robust person exhibiting fullness and a strong pulse can simply relieve the qi to self-recover from wheezing. In such cases, formulas like Kuaqing Yin, Sìchuāng Yin, Sìqī Decoction, Radish Seed Decoction, or Suzi Jiangqi Decoction are suitable. If there is stagnated qi in the Yangming channel leading to fullness, a mild purgative may be beneficial.[56p]

    　　　　　哮证治

    　　喘有夙根，通寒即发，或遇劳即发者，亦名哮喘。未发时以扶正气为主，既发时以攻邪气为主。扶正气者，须辨阴阳。除虚者补其阴，阳虚者补其阳。攻邪气须分微甚，或散其风，或温其寒，或清其痰火。然发久者气无不虚，故于消散中宜酌加温补，或于温补中宜量加消散。此等证候，当惓惓以元气为念，必使元气渐充，庶可望其渐愈。若攻之太过，未有不致日甚而危者。[57p]

    Treatment of Asthma

    Asthma has its deep-rooted origins, and can be triggered by cold or exertion; it is also referred to as wheezing and asthma. When it is not manifesting, one should primarily focus on reinforcing the vital energy; when it does manifest, the main focus should be on eliminating the pathogenic factors. To reinforce the vital energy, one must differentiate between yin and yang. If there is deficiency, one should tonify yin; if there is yang deficiency, one should tonify yang. To eliminate pathogenic factors, one must assess the severity; one may need to dispel wind, warm cold, or clear phlegm and heat. However, in chronic cases, the vital energy is invariably deficient, so during the process of dispelling, it is advisable to cautiously add warmth and tonification, or to appropriately increase the dispersing methods within the tonification. In such instances, one should always focus on nourishing the original qi, ensuring that it gradually fills up, for this gives hope for gradual recovery. If one excessively attacks, there has never been a case where it does not lead to worsening and danger.[57p]

    　　　　石室秘箓 【清　陈士铎】

    　　　　　喘病治法

    　　急治者，不可须臾缓也。如人忽感风邪，寒入乎肺经，以致一时喘急，抬肩大喘，气逆痰吐不出，又不能卧是也。方用柴胡，当归、黄芩、甘草、半夏、射干各一钱，桔梗、麦冬、茯苓各二钱，水煎服。此方妙在用柴胡、射干、桔梗以舒发肺金之气，用半夏以祛痰，用黄芩以去火。盖外感寒邪，则内必变为热证，今用黄芩以清解之。然徒用黄芩，虽曰清火，转足以抑遏其火气，妙在用桔梗、射干、柴胡一派辛散之品，转足以消火灭邪，此急治之一法。[58p]

    Secret Formula of the Stone Chamber
    By Chen Shiduo of the Qing Dynasty

    Treatment for Wheezing

    For urgent treatment, one must not delay even for a moment. When a person suddenly catches a wind-imbalance, and cold enters the lung meridian, it can lead to immediate wheezing, raised shoulders, labored breathing, and difficulty in expelling phlegm, making it impossible to lie down. The prescription includes one cash each of Chai Hu, Dang Gui, Huang Qin, Gan Cao, Ban Xia, and She Gan, and two cash each of Jie Geng, Mai Dong, and Fu Ling, to be decocted and taken. This formula excels in using Chai Hu, She Gan, and Jie Geng to disseminate and release the lung's vital energy, employing Ban Xia to eliminate phlegm, and using Huang Qin to clear heat. When one is externally invaded by cold, it must internally transform into a heat syndrome; thus, Huang Qin is used for its cleansing and resolving properties. However, using only Huang Qin, while it is said to clear heat, may inadvertently suppress the fire energy. The brilliance lies in the combination of Jie Geng, She Gan, and Chai Hu, which are warming and dispersive, effectively extinguishing fire and eliminating the pathogen. This is one method for urgent treatment.[58p]

    　　凡人有气喘不得卧，吐痰如泉涌者，舌不燥而喘不甚，一卧则喘，如此非外感之风邪，乃肾中之寒气也。盖肾中无火，则水无所养，乃上泛而为痰，将胃中之水，尽助其汹涌之势，而不可止遏矣。法当用六味丸汤加附子、肉桂大剂饮之，则肾宫火热，而水有所归，水既归宫，喘逆之气，亦下安而可卧。盖人之卧，必得肾气与肺气相交，而后河车之路，平安无奔逆也。方中补其肾火，何以安然能卧？不知肾为肺之子，子安则母亦宁。肺金之气，可归于肾宫，以养其耗散之气矣，此所以补肾火，正所以养肺金也。[59p]

    When a person experiences breathlessness and cannot lie down, and their phlegm flows out like a spring, yet their tongue is not dry and the breathlessness is not severe, lying down exacerbates the condition. This is not due to external causative wind but rather the cold energy within the kidneys. When there is no fire in the kidneys, the water has nothing to nourish it, rising up and causing phlegm. The water in the stomach then assists this surging force and cannot be stopped. The proper treatment is to use the Six Flavor Pill Decoction with the addition of a large dose of aconite and cinnamon, which will heat the kidney palace, allowing the water to return. Once the water returns to the palace, the breathlessness will subside and the person can lie down peacefully. For a person to sleep, the kidney energy and lung energy must interact; only then can the pathway be smooth and free from chaos. In the prescription, nourishing kidney fire allows for peaceful sleep. It is important to note that the kidney is the mother of the lung; when the child is at peace, the mother is also tranquil. The lung's metallic energy can return to the kidney palace to nourish its dissipating energy. Hence, nourishing kidney fire is truly a means to also nourish the lung's metal.[59p]

    况六味丸全是补肾水之神剂乎？水火同补，而肺金更安，肺肾相安，有不卧之而甚适者乎？　　喘证不同，有虚喘，有实喘。实喘看其证若重而实轻，用黄芩二钱，麦冬三钱，甘草五分，柴胡、苏叶、山豆根、半夏、乌药各一钱，水煎服，一剂喘止，不必再服也。然实证之喘气太急，喉必作声，肩必抬起，非若虚喘气少急而喉无声，肩不抬也。虚喘乃肾气大虚，而脾气又复将绝，故奔冲而上，欲绝尚未绝也。[60p]

    Is the Liu Wei Di Huang Wan truly a miraculous remedy for nourishing kidney essence? It balances water and fire, providing stability to the lung's metal element; when the lungs and kidneys are harmonized, is there anyone who cannot sleep soundly yet feels very comfortable?

    There are different types of wheezing; some are due to deficiency, while others are due to excess. For excess wheezing, if the symptoms appear heavy and are less pronounced, use two qian of Huang Qin, three qian of Mai Dong, five fen of Gan Cao, and one qian each of Chai Hu, Su Ye, Shan Dou Gen, Ban Xia, and Wu Yao. Decoction in water and consume; one dose will stop the wheezing, and no further doses are necessary. However, in cases of wheezing due to excess, the breath is often rapid, the throat makes noise, and the shoulders lift—unlike deficient wheezing, which is less urgent, with a silent throat and relaxed shoulders. Deficient wheezing indicates significant kidney deficiency, with the spleen’s energy on the verge of collapse, hence the urgent upward surges that struggle to break through but have not yet done so.[60p]

    方用救绝止喘汤，人参、熟地各一两，山茱萸、白芥子各三钱，麦冬五钱，五味子、牛膝各一钱，水煎服。一剂轻，二剂喘止，十剂全愈。此病实死证也，幸几微之气，留连于上下之间，若用凉药以平火，是速其亡也。然用桂附以补火，亦速其亡。盖气将绝之时，宜缓续而不宜骤续，譬如炉中火绝，止存星星之火，宜用薪炭引之。若遽投之以硫黄之类，反灭其火矣。更以寒凉之物动之，鲜有生气矣。方中妙在一派补肾补肺之药，与人参同用，则直入于至阴之中而生其气，肾气生而肺气亦生，自能接续于无何有之乡。况人参又上生肺以助肾之母，子母相生，更能救绝也。[61p]

    The formula to alleviate severe breathlessness contains the following ingredients: one tael each of ginseng and prepared rehmannia, three qian each of shan zhu yu and white mustard seed, five qian of ophiopogon, one qian each of schisandra and achyranthes. Brew with water and take. One dose may provide slight relief, two doses can stop wheezing, and ten doses can lead to full recovery. This condition is indeed a sign of imminent death; fortunately, a faint breath lingers in the upper and lower realms. If cool medicines are used to balance the fire, it hastens their demise. Similarly, using cinnamon and aconite to supplement the fire will also accelerate the end. When the vital energy approaches extinction, it should be gently supported, not urgently restored, just like a dying fire that still has a few embers—kindling it with firewood is advisable. If one abruptly throws sulfur or similar substances onto it, the fire will be extinguished. Moreover, using cold and cool substances to stir it leads to a rare chance of renewal. The brilliance of this formula lies in its combination of kidney and lung tonics. When used together with ginseng, it directly penetrates the very essence of yin, giving rise to kidney energy, which in turn generates lung energy, thus sustaining life in the realm of nothingness. Furthermore, ginseng nourishes the lungs to support the kidneys, promoting a mutual generation that can truly save one from death.[61p]

    Complete Collection of Ancient and Modern Books, Volume 284: Asthma Section

    Formulas

    Yue Bi Jia Ban Xia Decoction (by Zhong Jing, the same below)
    For treating asthma.
    Ingredients: 6 liang of Ma Huang, 0.5 jin each of Shi Gao and Ban Xia, 1 liang of Gan Cao, 3 liang of Sheng Jiang, 15 Da Zao.
    Preparation: Combine the six ingredients with 6 sheng of water; first boil Ma Huang to remove the froth, then add the other herbs and boil down to 3 sheng. Divide into three warm doses.

    Xiao Qing Long Decoction
    For water-induced asthma, particularly effective.
    Ingredients: 3 liang of Ma Huang (without joints), 3 liang of Shao Yao, 3 liang of roasted Gan Cao, 3 liang of Rou Gui, 3 liang of Pao Jiang, 3 liang of Xi Xin, 2 liang of Wu Wei Zi, 2.5 liang of Ban Xia soaked seven times.
    Preparation: Grind finely, take 3 qian at a time, and boil down to 7 parts. Take after meals.

    Xiao Qing Long Jia Shi Gao Decoction
    For treating asthma.
    Ingredients: 2 liang of Shi Gao, 3 qian each of Ma Huang, Shao Yao, Gui Zhi, Xi Xin, Gan Cao, and Gan Jiang; 0.5 sheng each of Wu Wei Zi and Ban Xia.
    Preparation: Combine the nine ingredients with 10 dou of water; first boil Ma Huang to remove the froth, then add the other herbs and boil down to 3 sheng. Strong individuals should take 1 sheng, while those weaker should reduce the amount, taken three times a day. For children, reduce to four doses.[62p]

    　　平气散 【东垣，下同】 　治喘。　　白牵牛二两，半生半炒，取头末一半　青皮去白　鸡心槟榔各三钱　陈皮去白，半两　大黄七钱　　右为细末，每服三钱，生姜汤一盏调下，无时。《内经》曰：肺苦气上逆，急食苦以泻之，白牵牛苦寒，泻气分湿热，上攻喘满，故以为君。陈皮苦温。体轻浮，理肺气；青皮苦辛平，散肺中滞气，故以为臣。槟榔辛温，性沉重，下痰降气；大黄苦寒，荡涤满实，故以为使也。
    　　木防己汤 【仲景，下同】 　治喘。　　木防己三两　石膏鸡子大一块　桂枝二两　人参四两　　右四味，以水六升，煎取二升，分温再服。

    Pinging Qi San
    For treating asthma.
    2 taels of white Qianqiu, half raw and half fried, take the first half of the head;
    3 qian each of Qingpi and chicken heart betel nut;
    half a tael of Chenpi, white removed;
    7 qian of Dahuang.
    The above comprises a fine powder. Take 3 qian each dose, with one cup of ginger decoction to mix, at any time. The Inner Canon states: "The lungs suffer from excess qi rising, urgently consume bitterness to drain it." White Qianqiu is bitter and cold, draining qi and expelling damp heat, hence its use as the chief ingredient. Chenpi is bitter and warm, light and floating, regulating lung qi; Qingpi is bitter and pungent, dispersing stagnant lung qi, hence its role as the minister. Betel nut is pungent and warm, with a heavy nature, descending phlegm and qi. Dahuang is bitter and cold, purging fullness and excess, thus it serves as the messenger.

    Mufangji Decoction
    For treating asthma.
    3 taels of Mufangji;
    1 large piece of gypsum the size of a chicken egg;
    2 taels of Gui Zhi;
    4 taels of Ren Shen.
    The above four ingredients, boiled in 6 sheng of water to obtain 2 sheng, divided and taken warm twice.

    Mufangji Decoction with Poria and Mangxiao
    For treating asthma.
    2 taels each of Mufangji and Gui Zhi;
    4 qian each of Ren Shen and Poria;
    3 he of Mangxiao.
    The above five ingredients, boiled in 6 sheng of water to obtain 2 sheng, remove dregs, add Mangxiao and slightly re-boil, then take warm again. If there is a slight purging effect, one is cured.

    Tingli Dazao Lung-Draining Decoction
    For treating lung abscess, chest fullness and swelling, shortness of breath, generalized body and facial swelling, nasal obstruction, heavy voice, and inability to distinguish scents.
    Tingli as needed, fry until yellow.[63p]

    　　右件细研，丸如弹子大。水三盏，枣十枚，煎一盏，去枣入药，煎七分，食后服。法令先投小青龙汤三服，乃进此药，即《济生》葶苈散，汤使不同。《济生》方：炒甜葶苈、桔梗、(艹舌)蒌子、薏苡仁、升麻、桑皮、葛根各一两，炙甘草半两。

    　　右为细末，姜汁蒸饼为丸如桐子大。每服三五十丸，姜汤下。小儿丸如米大。[64p]

    The following is a translation of the provided Classical Chinese text:

    The above should be finely ground into pills the size of a bullet. Use three cups of water and ten jujubes; boil to one cup, remove the jujubes, and boil the medicine until reduced to seven portions, then take after meals. The method requires first taking three doses of Xiao Qing Long Decoction, and then proceeding with this medicine, which is the Ting Li San from "Ji Sheng." The decoction is different from the one in "Ji Sheng": the ingredients are one tael each of roasted sweet tingli, jie geng, (caoshe) luozi, yi yi ren, sheng ma, sang pi, and ge gen, with half a tael of honey-fried licorice.

    Qian Kun Decoction [from "Fu Ren Da Quan"] treats wheezing with wind phlegm. Use seven pieces of banxia, processed and broken into four pieces; remove the skin and string from the soap pod; one inch each of honey-fried licorice and fresh ginger of finger size. Combine with one cup of water, boil down to half, and take in one dose. Another formula omits licorice, using only one tael of banxia powder and half a tael of soap pod, along with seven pieces of ginger, all placed in a cloth bag. Use three sheng (approximately 9 cups) of water, boil until reduced to one cup and five portions, hand massage to extract clear juice, divide into three doses, and take two doses for effect.

    Banxia Pills [from "Bao Ming Ji"] treat wheezing and phlegm caused by wind, with the urge to vomit and nausea. Use one tael of banxia and three qian each of betel nut and realgar. Grind finely, mix with ginger juice to make pills the size of tung seeds. For each dose, take thirty to fifty pills with ginger soup. For children, make pills the size of rice.[64p]

    　　定喘饼子 【《宝鉴》】
    　　芫花酢浸一宿炒　桑白皮炒　吴茱萸炒　马兜铃　陈皮去白，各一两　寒食面三两　白牵牛三两，半生半炒，取头末二两　　右为末，和匀滴水，丸如樱桃大，捏饼子，取热灰半碗，在碗内同炒饼子热，每夜服一饼嚼烂，煎马兜铃汤下。如患人心头不快，加上一饼或二饼，至微明利下，神效。妇人有胎者，不可服。

    Ding Chuan Bingzi (Anti-Asthma Cake)
    Yuanhua Vinegar soaked overnight and then fried, mulberry bark fried, evodia fried, Aristolochia, and aged tangerine peel (white part removed), each one liang; cold food flour three liang; white bindweed three liang, half raw and half fried, take two liang of the head and tail. Combine these into a powder, mix with water, roll into balls the size of cherries, and flatten them. Take half a bowl of hot ash, stir the cakes in it to heat. Every night, consume one cake, chewing it thoroughly, and drink it down with a decoction of Aristolochia. If the patient feels discomfort in the heart, add one or two more cakes until slight relief is felt; the effect is miraculous. Women who are pregnant should not take this.

    Mai Men Dong Tang (Ophiopogon Decoction)
    For treating deficiency-related wheezing.
    Seven sheng of Ophiopogon, one sheng of Pinellia, four taels of ginseng, two taels of licorice, three he of polished rice, twelve dates.
    Use these six ingredients with twelve liters of water, decoct until six liters remain, and take one liter warm three times a day, and once at night.

    Ren Shen Ping Fei San (Ginseng Lung-Soothing Powder)
    For heat-induced wheezing in the lungs.
    Fried mulberry bark, two qian; Anemarrhena, one and a half qian; fried licorice; Poria; ginseng; Rehmannia peel; Asparagus (heart removed), each one qian; green peel and aged tangerine peel, each six fen; thirty berries of Schisandra, crushed.
    Use two bowls of water, five slices of fresh ginger, decoct to one bowl, take warm after meals. If heat is severe, add one qian each of Scutellaria and peppermint leaves.[65p]

    JiajianXie Bai San (from "Fa Ming")
    Treats conditions with yin qi below and yang qi above, causing cough, vomiting, and wheezing.

    Ding Chuan Qi Fang
    Treats thick phlegm congestion in those who are heavy and wheeze.
    Components:

    • 2 liang of tangerine peel
    • 5 qian of alum (stir-fried until fragrant, discard alum)
    • 1 liang each of pinellia, apricot seeds (stir-fried with bran), and Areca seed (oil removed)
    • 7 qian of roasted licorice
    • 5 qian of yellow quino mixed with wine and dried
    • 3 qian of soapberry (skin and strings removed, burnt to ash)

After taking for 3 to 5 days, thick phlegm will be expelled in stools, leading to recovery. Weak individuals should take 7 fen.[66p]

    Wrinkled Lung Pill - For Treating Wheezing
    (Ingredients) Winter Flower, Anemarrhena, Gentian, Hundred Parts, Purple Aster Fungi, Fritillaria, Donkey-hide Gelatine, Roasted Glutinous Rice, each one tael; Almonds with skin removed, ground to a fine powder, four taels. Combine these ingredients to make a powder. Take one sheep's lung, wash it with water to see how much it can hold, and add a bit more water in accordance with its capacity. Boil the almonds until bubbling, strain, and pour into the lung, securely fasten it. Cook the glutinous rice water until done, grind to a fine paste, and mix with the previous powder, pound thousands of times into balls the size of a tung seed. Take fifty balls, consumed before meals with decoction of mulberry white skin.

    Proven Secret Formula [from "Zheng Chuan"] - For Treating Long-term Wheezing.
    One liter of mulberry wood insect feces, roasted; Almonds with skin removed, roasted; Radish seeds, roasted, each half a jin (500 grams); Licorice, two taels. Grind all together into a very fine powder. Soak in broth to form into pills the size of a tung seed. Take fifty to seventy pills with light ginger broth.

Chew these and add three sheng (6.3 liters) of water, boil down to one sheng, discard the residue, and take warm in three doses.     Gui Ling Wu Wei Gan Cao Decoction: This formula treats dyspnea. Use 4 ounces each of cinnamon twig and poria, 3 ounces of honey-fried licorice, and half a sheng of Schisandra fruit.     Zhen Ying Powder: This formula is used for prolonged acute dyspnea that causes insomnia and has not responded to numerous remedies. Take 4 ounces of clear white quartz, place it in a raw silk bag, and put it inside a male pig's stomach. Sew it shut and boil until cooked, then remove the medicine. Replace the pig's stomach and repeat the boiling process three times. After cooking, dry the medicine and grind it into powder. To this powder, add 2 qian of Guanjue (caowei) Donghua Powder, 2 qian of the medicine powder, 2 inches of mulberry bark, 3 slices of fresh ginger, 1 jujube, and 1.5 sheng of water. Boil until reduced to 7 parts, and take orally. The pig's stomach can also be consumed, but must not be seasoned with vinegar, sauce, salt, pepper, ginger, etc. The formula for Guanjue Donghua Powder includes 1 qian of Guanjue Donghua, 2 qian each of fritillary bulb, anemarrhena, mulberry leaves, apricot kernels, pinellia, donkey-hide gelatin, and licorice, plus 4 qian of ephedra without stems, coarsely ground.[69p]

    Simple Yellow Pill
    Dissolves phlegm, regulates breathing, and relieves nasal congestion.
    Fine powder of realgar and orpiment, each one qian; seven pieces of gardenia fruit; forty-nine grains of mung bean; one character of white arsenic, finely ground and used raw.
    Mix these into a powder and form into pills the size of mung beans. Take one or two pills with cool mint tea before bed.

    Clear Golden Elixir
    Treats food accumulation, phlegm blockage, wheezing, and coughs, especially when triggered by rich flavors.
    One liang of cleaned and steamed radish seeds, powdered; three qian of roasted soapberry pods to be retained.
    Soak the above in fresh ginger juice, steam, and form into pills the size of small mung beans. Take three to fifty pills, swallowing them. For sudden wheezing, make pills the size of walnuts with ginger juice and honey. Take seventy to eighty pills, sucking on them to stop wheezing.
    Additionally, this recipe is for chronic or recent cases of wheezing and cough.

    Cicada Shells (Footless)
    Finely ground light powder; one liang of Aristolochia; five qian each of realgar, frankincense, and peeled apricot kernels (with pointed ends and doubles); five qian of raw arsenic; forty-nine grains of light fermented soybeans.
    Mix this into a powder with natural juice of fresh ginger and plantago, and form into pills the size of small marbles. Take one pill, chew well, and follow with ginger soup before bed.[70p]

    Treatment for Cough and Wheezing

    • 2 qian of Suzi, 麻黄 (Ephedra) without branches, (艹款) Donghua (Winter Flower), honey-roasted mulberry leaves, and Banxia (Pinellia) each 3 qian; peeled apricot kernels, and licorice each 1.5 qian; 21 pieces of white fruit (ginkgo), shelled and stir-fried until yellow.

    Ding Chuan Decoction - Stops all wheezing.

    • 21 pieces of white fruit, shelled and chopped, stir-fried until yellow; 1 qian of licorice; 2 qian of Suzi; 麻黄 (Ephedra) without branches, (艹款) Donghua (Winter Flower), and honey-roasted mulberry bark, each 3 qian; peeled apricot kernels and Huangqin (Scutellaria) stir-fried, each 1 qian.
    • Use 3 sheng of water, boil down to 2 sheng, divide into two doses (do not use ginger), and take gradually, at any time.

    Jian Xian Pill - Treats coughing and wheezing caused by injury from salty cold food and drink.

    Nine-Flavored Decoction
    For treating cold-induced asthma. Cold asthma is characterized by cold hands and feet, with a deep and subtle pulse.

    Zi Jin Dan (The Purple Gold Pill)

    From "Entering the Door": For asthma that does not allow lying down, it can only be taken after three years.

    • 1 qian of arsenic powder
    • 1 liang of crushed plain fermented soybeans
    • 4 liang of finely chopped fresh pig's blood

    Mix these three ingredients, divide into three portions, wrap each portion in paper and clay, dry it in the oven until the clay is dry. Then, use charcoal fire to roast until the blue smoke is completely exhausted. Leave it on the ground overnight to expel the toxic smoke, then ground into powder. Soak in water to form dough, and make small pills the size of mung beans. After eating, wash down with cool tea. For adults, take 20 pills; for children, 7 pills. Avoid all salty foods and soups.

    From "Returning to Spring": Whenever the weather threatens to rain, you may experience coughing and wheezing, making sitting or lying down uncomfortable, and loss of appetite. This indicates that there is cold phlegm accumulated in the lung orifices, which invades through the mouth and nose with the cold air from overcast weather, causing the lungs to expand with sound. This condition can cause lifelong suffering, and it may also be hereditary. Each episode should be treated promptly; after seven or eight instances, if the phlegm is foul-smelling and you expel white phlegm, this will eradicate the root of the problem.

    • 1 qian of white arsenic, to be ground anew
    • 3 qian of burnt alum, to be ground anew
    • 1 liang of plain fermented soybeans, soaked in water, peeled, steamed, and ground into paste

    Mix the above powders, roll into pills the size of mung beans. Take 5 pills with cool tea; for severe cases, take 9 pills. The aim is to stop wheezing to be considered cured, and there is no need to take more. Long-term use will surely yield results.[79p]

    Deadly Pill by Danxi
    Treats wheezing and breathlessness.
    1 qian of arsenic, 2 qian of white alum, 3 qian of white aconite, 4 qian of southern star, 5 qian of pinellia.
    First, calcine the arsenic and alum in a stone vessel until red, then withdraw when it turns yellow. Do not let it touch iron. Mix with the remaining powdered herbs uniformly, and form into pills the size of millet using a ginger juice and flour paste. Coat with red mercury. Take seven pills, or three for children, swallowed with well water. Avoid hot and toxic foods. This formula treats phlegm and wheezing emergencies. Once the illness is resolved, one may then use a mixture of Anemarrhena and Poria soup, ginseng and five-flavor powder, and nourishing lung soup to replenish deficiency.

    Established Powder (source: "Medical Mirror", the same applies below)
    A secret formula for treating asthma.
    One large soapberry pod, split open to remove seeds, insert the flesh of the croton nut, tie securely with iron wire, and char until yellow. Each qian is combined with half a qian each of pinellia and almonds, cooked in fragrant oil until yellow. Grind into a fine powder. For each persimmon cake, take one qian of the powder, chew well, and swallow with warm water.[80p]

    　　大百劳散 【河间，下同】 　治一切劳疾肌劣，喘息不卧，痰涎不食。　　蛤蚧一对，蜜炙　鳖甲一个，去裙酢炙　附子　人参　柴胡　干姜　白茯苓　白朮　茴香　青皮去白　杏仁去皮尖　知母　贝母　官桂　甘草炙　半夏生姜制　苍朮汤浸，各一两　苏木　龙胆草各半两　　右为末，每服二钱，水一盏，用生姜三片、枣二枚、乌梅二枚同煎，空心稍热服。有汗加小麦二十粒。不用铁煎。

    Great Bai Lao San
    Treats all labor-induced ailments, weakness of the muscles, shortness of breath with inability to lie down, and phlegm preventing eating.
    Take a pair of gecko, honey-roasted; one turtle shell, roasted after removing the skirt; Aconite; Ginseng; Bupleurum; Dried Ginger; White Poria; Bai Zhu; Fennel; Green tangerine peel without white part; Almonds without skin and tip; Anemarrhena; Fritillaria; Cinnamon; Honey-roasted Licorice; Prepared Pinellia with Ginger; and soaked in Cang Zhu decoction, each one tael; Su Mu and Gentian each half a tael.
    Grind these into a powder. Each dose is two qián, mixed with water, using three slices of fresh ginger, two jujubes, and two black plums boiled together, taken warm on an empty stomach. If there is sweating, add twenty grains of wheat. Do not boil with iron.

    Little Bai Lao San
    Treats persistent labor-induced cough and spontaneous sweating.
    Stir-fry millet husk without limit.
    Grind this into a powder, each dose is two qián, boiled with black plum in one cup of water, taken warm. If there is sweating after eating, add thirty grains of wheat, boil together, and take warm.

    Neijin Wan
    Treats asthma.
    Twenty-one chicken gizzards; two and a half qián of stone; half a tael of yellow lead.
    Grind these finely, expose to dew for seven nights, then add half a tael of white morning glory powder, half a tael of lepidium powder, and two and a half qián of Pinellia powder, mix well, then use steamed jujube flesh to form pills the size of sesame seeds, expose to dew for two nights, and coat with cinnabar powder. Each dose is seven pills, taken with cold tea just before sleep.[81p]

    喘息方

    To treat lung heat, with symptoms of chest congestion and shortness of breath, to relieve qi and eliminate heat.

    Ingredients:

    • Gypsum: 8 taels
    • Bai Qian (a herb): 3 taels
    • Apricot kernels: 3 taels
    • Red honey: 7 heaped sections
    • Tangerine peel: 5 taels
    • Bai Zhu (a herb): 5 taels
    • Goji root bark, cut: 2 sheng

    Method:
    Crush the seven ingredients, use 7 sheng of water, boil until 2 sheng remain, strain, add honey, boil three times, and divide into three doses.

    Another formula to treat lung heat, with symptoms of cough, shortness of breath, and expectoration of pus and blood:

    Ingredients:

    • Fresh Rehmannia, cut: 2 sheng
    • Gypsum: 8 taels
    • Ephedra: 5 taels
    • Genus Asarum and Antelope horn: 3 taels each
    • Glauber's salt: 3 taels
    • Apricot kernels: 4 taels
    • Red honey: 1 sheng
    • Fresh bamboo leaves: 1 egg-sized quantity

    Method:
    Crush the nine ingredients, use 7 sheng of water, boil until 2 sheng remain, strain, add honey, boil two times, and divide into three doses.

    Tangerine Peel Decoction

    To treat lung heat with upward gas, cough, and shortness of breath.

    Ingredients:

    • Tangerine peel: 3 taels
    • Ephedra: 3 taels
    • Chai Hu (Bupleurum): 3 taels
    • Dried purple mint: 3 taels
    • Fermented wheat: 4 taels
    • Apricot kernels: 4 taels
    • Gypsum: 8 taels

    Method:
    Crush the seven ingredients, use 9 sheng of water, boil Ephedra twice, skim off foam, add remaining herbs, boil until 3 sheng remain, strain, and divide into three doses. If not improved, take two more doses.

    Notes: Dried Purple Mint can be substituted with Dried Blue.

    Xie Fei San treats fatigue from drinking, or when exposed to the wind; it helps with the emotional disturbances that affect the lungs, causing facial yellowing and swelling, dizziness upon rising, coughing, shortness of breath, and a feeling of sudden suffocation. There may be a tightness in the heart area, inability to eat or drink, and possibly vomiting pus or blood, with chest pain radiating to the back, a feeling of fullness and nausea.

    Wu Wei Zi and Bai Bu, each two and a half taels; Fu Ling, Fu Zi, Cistanches, Dang Gui, Shi Hu, Yuan Zhi, Xu Duan, each one tael; Xi Xin and Gan Cao, each seven fen; Fang Feng, Shu Jiao, Zi Wan, Gui Xin, (草款) Dong Hua, and Gan Jiang, each one and a half taels; peach kernels, peeled and sharpened, sixty pieces; almond kernels, peeled and sharpened, thirty pieces.

    The above nineteen ingredients are to be ground and taken with wine by the spoonful, three times a day, gradually increasing to two spoonfuls.[83p]

    Hua Gai San
    For treating the coldness and dampness affecting the lungs, leading to wheezing, shortness of breath, and inability to sleep or loss of voice.
    Ingredients:

    • Bitter almonds, peeled and roasted, 1 ounce
    • Perilla seeds, lightly roasted, 1 ounce
    • Ephedra, roots removed, 1 ounce
    • Red Poria, 1 ounce
    • Dried tangerine peel, 1 ounce
    • White mulberry bark, scorched, 1 ounce
    • Licorice, winter scorched, half an ounce

    Grind these into a fine powder. Take 2 qian (6 grams) with 1 cup of water, boil down to seven parts, and take warm after meals.

    Er Huang Wan
    For treating phlegm stagnation in the stomach, leading to wheezing and difficulty breathing.
    Ingredients:

    • Realgar (yellow arsenic), 1 qian (3 grams)
    • Orpiment (golden arsenic), 1 ounce

    Grind these two ingredients into an extremely fine powder, and melt with yellow wax to form pills the size of small pellets. Take one pill at midnight, with warm, freshly cooked glutinous rice porridge; stir and mix the medicine into the porridge while hot before consuming.

    Ren Shen Hu Tao Tang
    For treating fullness in the chest and breathlessness, making it difficult to sleep.
    Ingredients:

    • Ginseng, cut into thin slices, about 1 inch
    • Walnuts, 5 pieces, with the meat sliced

    Prepare these as one dose with 1 small cup of water and 5 slices of fresh ginger; boil down to seven parts, strain, and take warm before lying down.[85p]

    Almond Pills
    For chronic lung wheezing, persistent coughing, and inability to sleep, taking this will assuredly help.
    Remove the skin and tip of the almonds, equal parts walnut meat. Grind together into a paste, add a little refined honey, and shape into pills the size of a pellet. Take one or two pills each time, chew carefully, and swallow with ginger soup, after meals and before bed.
    For severe wheezing that feels life-threatening.

    Dahuang Decoction
    One ounce of rhubarb, wrap in damp paper and roast; two ounces of morning glory, stir-fried.
    Grind these into a powder, mix with honey water, and use two pennies worth to stop immediately. This formula treats upper heat and phlegm wheezing; it should not be used if there is lung deficiency with cold stomach.

    Huangqin Banxia Decoction
    Specifically treats cold enveloping heat and simultaneously addresses both exterior and interior conditions.
    Equal parts of Banxia, Zhike, Huangqin (wine-stir-fried), Jiegan, Zisu, Mahuang, Almonds, and Licorice.
    Add two cups of water, three slices of ginger, and one jujube, decoct until reduced to eight parts, taken far from meals. In cold weather, add cinnamon twig.

    Shen Ying Dan (from "Medical Forest")
    For treating cough and asthma.
    One measure of mung beans, one qian (about 3.3 grams).
    Take the two ingredients, place them in a sand pot, boil in water until the beans are soft, grind into a paste, dry and grind into powder again. Form them into pills the size of sesame seeds. Adults take thirty pills, children take fifteen, and those under seven take six or seven. Take them with cold tea before bed, avoiding hot foods for one day. This remedy is highly effective.

    Da Li Ge Wan
    For treating wind-phlegm obstruction, fullness with coughing, and wind attacking upwards.
    Two liang (about 60 grams) of Qián Qiú (morning glory seeds) powder, one liang each of green skin, betel nut, roasted soap pod (with skin and strings removed), and soaked banxia (pinellia); two and a half qian of wood fragrance; five qian of stir-fried sophora fruit.
    Grind these into powder, mix with ginger juice to form pills the size of wutong seeds. Each dose is fifty pills taken after meals with ginger soup.

    Zhen Yuan Yin: This formula treats shortness of breath that resembles wheezing, with rapid and hurried breathing, difficulty in raising oneself, inability to swallow, and obstruction of the airways, especially in critical situations. People commonly misinterpret this as merely breathlessness; however, the root cause lies in the extreme deficiency of the Liver and Kidney. This is caused by the failure of the body’s essential forces to interact, resulting in qi collapse. It is particularly prevalent among women with constant blood deficiency. This formula should be used urgently for recovery—it's truly an extraordinary remedy. When diagnosing this condition, the pulse is surely weak and without vitality. If weak and simultaneously tense, the situation is even more serious. If common people are unaware and mistakenly claim it's phlegm or qi stasis and use remedies such as Niu Huang, Su He, or Qing, Chen, and Zhi Ke for breaking qi, it will accelerate danger. Ingredients: 7-8 qian of Cooked Rehmannia (up to 1-2 liang for severe cases), 2-3 qian of Angelica, 1-2-3 qian of Honey-fried Licorice, 2 sheng of water, decoct to 8 parts, take warm.

    Liu'an Decoction: Treats wind-cold cough, initial sensations of non-wind, phlegm obstruction, and reversed qi.     Single Prescription

    For difficulty breathing due to water-induced panic from drinking cold water in youth: Use seven wen of large silver coins, seven white plums, and one chong of water; soak them together for three nights, take one sip on an empty stomach, and after a while, expectorate.

    For chronic and relentless lung deficiency causing wheezing: Use five qian of fresh milk powder that is bright, three liang of wax melted, mix and steam in a rice steamer until cooked, then grind into pills the size of a wutzi. Take one pill with warm water.

    For yang deficiency with wheezing, spontaneous sweating, shortness of breath, and dizziness: Use five qian of ginseng and one liang of熟附子(fully cooked fuzi), divided into four doses, each taken with ten slices of fresh ginger, with two cups of water boiled down to one cup, consume warm away from meals.

    For acute wheezing and difficulty in breathing: Use powdered ginseng, take a spoonful with soup five to six times daily.

    To calm wheezing and nourish the heart and kidney: Use Shenmi Powder. Ingredients: half a liang of white fairy grass, soaked in rice wash for three nights, dried and roasted; two and a half qian of ginseng; one and a half liang of fried ejiao; one liang of chicken's gizzard roasted into powder. Take two qian each time with sweet rice drink on an empty stomach, twice daily.[92p]

    　　痰喘气急：(艹舌)蒌二个，明矾一枣大，同烧存性研末，以熟萝卜蘸食，药尽病除。【《普济方》】

    　　远年近日喘嗽：用皂角不蛀者三大茎，刮去黑皮，刀切开去子，每子仓内，入巴豆肉一粒，合就以麻皮缚定，用生姜自然汁和蜜涂令周匝，慢火炙之，又涂又炙，以焦黄为度，劈开去巴豆不用；又以好明矾一两枯过，蓖麻子七粒，生姜汁和蜜再涂炙前皂角三味，同为末；却以杏仁二两去皮尖研成膏，却与前药和匀，每服一钱，用柿子干灸过，候冷点入药内，细嚼，临睡服。忌热毒鱼鲊鲑鮝油面酒米酢煎煿热物。[94p]

    Phlegm and wheezing: Take two loquats and a piece of alum the size of a jujube. Burn them together, grind into a powder, and dip cooked radish to consume. When the medicine is finished, the illness will be cured.

    Mysterious remedy for wheezing: Use two pig toenails, burn them to ash, and grind finely. Add one piece of musk and grind it finely together. Mix with wax tea to administer.

    For settling asthma and transforming phlegm: Use forty-nine pig toenails, clean and dry them. Inside each toenail, place one character of pinellia and one character of alum, then put them in a jar and seal tightly to prevent smoke from escaping. Fire-bake them until red, then remove from heat, grind finely, add musk, and take with a decoction of glutinous rice one qian; for children, take half a qian.

    For chronic and recent wheezing: Use three thick pods of soapwart without pests. Scrape off the black skin and cut open to remove the seeds. Inside each pod, place one seed of semei infiltrated with a piece of hemp cloth to bind.     Additionally, take one liang of good alum that has become dry, seven seeds of castor bean, and the ginger juice mixed with honey to coat the previously prepared soapwart ingredients, then grind them into a powder.

    Finally, take two liang of peeled apricot kernels and grind them into a paste, mixing well with the previous medicine. Each dose is one qian, applied with dried persimmon that has been roasted until cool before being added to the medicine. Chew finely and take before sleep.     　　肺经久受寒邪，喘急初发，则寒从背起，冷如冰霜，渐渐喘促，气不相续，痰涎壅塞，咯吐不出，坐卧不得，莫可支吾，两肩耸竖，曲背努目，困惫欲死，宜服。或未效，再服即愈，其效如神。用鲫鱼重一斤者，不去鳞肠，只于肚下近头处开一空，入信石一钱，令深入在内，却以鱼入竹筒内，外以青蒿盐泥固济候干，火煅竹筒通红，候冷去泥取鱼，去烧不过者研细，入蛤粉三钱，研和得所，丸如菉豆大，朱砂为衣，每服三五丸，临卧用冷沙糖水送下。忌热物。一方正喘急时宜服，不可多过丸数。欲试此药，用猪肺一枚吹胀，入此药数丸于肺脘内，顷刻渐痿，方表其功。[95p]

    If the lung has long suffered from cold pathogens, the initial onset of wheezing will feel as if cold rises from the back, cold like ice and frost, gradually leading to urgent breathing, with no continuity of breath. Phlegm and saliva become obstructed, and one cannot expel them; sitting or lying down becomes impossible, leaving one unable to find relief. The shoulders rise and stiffen, the back curves, and the eyes strain, feeling exhausted as if wanting to die. It is advisable to take medicine. If the first dose is ineffective, taking it again will surely cure the condition, with results akin to magic.

    The preparation should be made with a pound of crucian carp, without removing the scales or intestines, but making an opening near the head region. Place a small amount of mineral substance inside, ensuring it goes deep. Then, put the fish in a bamboo tube, coating the outside with a mixture of mugwort and salt to seal it. Heat the bamboo tube until it glows red, then allow it to cool, removing the mud to extract the fish. Simply grind this, not burning it, then mix in three taels of clam powder, grind until well combined, and form into pills the size of a mung bean. Coat them with vermilion.

    Take three to five pills at bedtime, washed down with cold sugar water. Avoid hot substances. This remedy is suitable when experiencing acute wheezing; do not exceed the recommended number of pills. If you wish to test this medicine, take a pig's lung and inflate it, placing a few pills inside the lung, and shortly thereafter, it will gradually weaken, demonstrating its efficacy.[95p]

    　　治喘嗽上气，一切肺喘剧甚者，效如神：用蒲颓叶焙碾为细末，米饮调服二钱，上并服取差。气味清香，其实酸濇，夏红可食，核如枣核□类山茱萸，拣叶背白者用，江西谓之卢都子。【《中藏经》】

    To treat wheezing and coughing, especially severe lung wheezing, this is effective like a divine remedy: use finely ground dried leaves of the plant known as "Pu Tai" (or similar), mixed with rice drink; take two qian (a measure) at once. The taste is fragrant and actually sour. The summer red variety is edible, with seeds similar to jujube pits, specifically choose those with white undersides. In Jiangxi, it is called "Lu Du Zi."

    For cold phlegm causing coughing: take juice from wild coriander mixed with wine and drink to stop the cough.
